<PlainText>
<Line number="2824">No, by my soul; I never in my life</Line>
<Line number="2825">Did hear a challenge urged more modestly,</Line>
<Line number="2826">Unless a brother should a brother dare</Line>
<Line number="2827">To gentle exercise and proof of arms.</Line>
<Line number="2828">He gave you all the duties of a man;</Line>
<Line number="2829">Trimm'd up your praises with a princely tongue,</Line>
<Line number="2830">Spoke to your deservings like a chronicle,</Line>
<Line number="2831">Making you ever better than his praise</Line>
<Line number="2832">By still dispraising praise valued in you;</Line>
<Line number="2833">And, which became him like a prince indeed,</Line>
<Line number="2834">He made a blushing cital of himself;</Line>
<Line number="2835">And chid his truant youth with such a grace</Line>
<Line number="2836">As if he master'd there a double spirit.</Line>
<Line number="2837">Of teaching and of learning instantly.</Line>
<Line number="2838">There did he pause: but let me tell the world,</Line>
<Line number="2839">If he outlive the envy of this day,</Line>
<Line number="2840">England did never owe so sweet a hope,</Line>
<Line number="2841">So much misconstrued in his wantonness.</Line>
</PlainText>

<Line number="3039">O, Harry, thou hast robb'd me of my youth!</Line>
<Line number="3040">I better brook the loss of brittle life</Line>
<Line number="3041">Than those proud titles thou hast won of me;</Line>
<Line number="3042">They wound my thoughts worse than sword my flesh:</Line>
<Line number="3043">
But thought's the slave of life, and life time's fool;
</Line>
<Line number="3044">And time, that takes survey of all the world,</Line>
<Line number="3045">Must have a stop. O, I could prophesy,</Line>
<Line number="3046">But that the earthy and cold hand of death</Line>
<Line number="3047">Lies on my tongue: no, Percy, thou art dust</Line>
<Line number="3048">And food for--</Line>

<PlainText>
<Line number="3050">
For worms, brave Percy: fare thee well, great heart!
</Line>
<Line number="3051">Ill-weaved ambition, how much art thou shrunk!</Line>
<Line number="3052">When that this body did contain a spirit,</Line>
<Line number="3053">A kingdom for it was too small a bound;</Line>
<Line number="3054">But now two paces of the vilest earth</Line>
<Line number="3055">Is room enough: this earth that bears thee dead</Line>
<Line number="3056">Bears not alive so stout a gentleman.</Line>
<Line number="3057">If thou wert sensible of courtesy,</Line>
<Line number="3058">I should not make so dear a show of zeal:</Line>
<Line number="3059">But let my favours hide thy mangled face;</Line>
<Line number="3060">And, even in thy behalf, I'll thank myself</Line>
<Line number="3061">For doing these fair rites of tenderness.</Line>
<Line number="3062">Adieu, and take thy praise with thee to heaven!</Line>
<Line number="3063">Thy ignominy sleep with thee in the grave,</Line>
<Line number="3064">But not remember'd in thy epitaph!</Line>
<Line number="3065">[He spieth FALSTAFF on the ground]</Line>
<Line number="3066">What, old acquaintance! could not all this flesh</Line>
<Line number="3067">Keep in a little life? Poor Jack, farewell!</Line>
<Line number="3068">I could have better spared a better man:</Line>
<Line number="3069">O, I should have a heavy miss of thee,</Line>
<Line number="3070">If I were much in love with vanity!</Line>
<Line number="3071">Death hath not struck so fat a deer to-day,</Line>
<Line number="3072">Though many dearer, in this bloody fray.</Line>
<Line number="3073">Embowell'd will I see thee by and by:</Line>
<Line number="3074">Till then in blood by noble Percy lie.</Line>
</PlainText>

<Section>5</Section>
<PlainText>
<Line number="3076">
[Rising up] Embowelled! if thou embowel me to-day,
</Line>
<Line number="3077">I'll give you leave to powder me and eat me too</Line>
<Line number="3078">to-morrow. 'Sblood,'twas time to counterfeit, or</Line>
<Line number="3079">
that hot termagant Scot had paid me scot and lot too.
</Line>
<Line number="3080">Counterfeit? I lie, I am no counterfeit: to die,</Line>
<Line number="3081">is to be a counterfeit; for he is but the</Line>
<Line number="3082">
counterfeit of a man who hath not the life of a man:
</Line>
<Line number="3083">but to counterfeit dying, when a man thereby</Line>
<Line number="3084">liveth, is to be no counterfeit, but the true and</Line>
<Line number="3085">perfect image of life indeed. The better part of</Line>
<Line number="3086">valour is discretion; in the which better part I</Line>
<Line number="3087">have saved my life.'Zounds, I am afraid of this</Line>
<Line number="3088">gunpowder Percy, though he be dead: how, if he</Line>
<Line number="3089">should counterfeit too and rise? by my faith, I am</Line>
<Line number="3090">afraid he would prove the better counterfeit.</Line>
<Line number="3091">
Therefore I'll make him sure; yea, and I'll swear I
</Line>
<Line number="3092">killed him. Why may not he rise as well as I?</Line>
<Line number="3093">Nothing confutes me but eyes, and nobody sees me.</Line>
<Line number="3094">Therefore, sirrah,</Line>
<Line number="3095">[Stabbing him]</Line>
<Line number="3096">
with a new wound in your thigh, come you along with me.
</Line>
</PlainText>
<PhoneticText>

<PlainText>
<Line number="3141">Thus ever did rebellion find rebuke.</Line>
<Line number="3142">Ill-spirited Worcester! did not we send grace,</Line>
<Line number="3143">Pardon and terms of love to all of you?</Line>
<Line number="3144">And wouldst thou turn our offers contrary?</Line>
<Line number="3145">Misuse the tenor of thy kinsman's trust?</Line>
<Line number="3146">Three knights upon our party slain to-day,</Line>
<Line number="3147">A noble earl and many a creature else</Line>
<Line number="3148">Had been alive this hour,</Line>
<Line number="3149">If like a Christian thou hadst truly borne</Line>
<Line number="3150">Betwixt our armies true intelligence.</Line>
</PlainText>

<PlainText>
<Line number="3158">The noble Scot, Lord Douglas, when he saw</Line>
<Line number="3159">The fortune of the day quite turn'd from him,</Line>
<Line number="3160">The noble Percy slain, and all his men</Line>
<Line number="3161">Upon the foot of fear, fled with the rest;</Line>
<Line number="3162">And falling from a hill, he was so bruised</Line>
<Line number="3163">That the pursuers took him. At my tent</Line>
<Line number="3164">The Douglas is; and I beseech your grace</Line>
<Line number="3165">I may dispose of him.</Line>
</PlainText>

<Line number="3167">Then, brother John of Lancaster, to you</Line>
<Line number="3168">This honourable bounty shall belong:</Line>
<Line number="3169">Go to the Douglas, and deliver him</Line>
<Line number="3170">Up to his pleasure, ransomless and free:</Line>
<Line number="3171">His valour shown upon our crests to-day</Line>
<Line number="3172">Hath taught us how to cherish such high deeds</Line>
<Line number="3173">Even in the bosom of our adversaries.</Line>
</PlainText>

<Section>5</Section>
<PlainText>
<Line number="3176">Then this remains, that we divide our power.</Line>
<Line number="3177">You, son John, and my cousin Westmoreland</Line>
<Line number="3178">
Towards York shall bend you with your dearest speed,
</Line>
<Line number="3179">To meet Northumberland and the prelate Scroop,</Line>
<Line number="3180">Who, as we hear, are busily in arms:</Line>
<Line number="3181">Myself and you, son Harry, will towards Wales,</Line>
<Line number="3182">To fight with Glendower and the Earl of March.</Line>
<Line number="3183">Rebellion in this land shall lose his sway,</Line>
<Line number="3184">Meeting the cheque of such another day:</Line>
<Line number="3185">And since this business so fair is done,</Line>
<Line number="3186">Let us not leave till all our own be won.</Line>
</PlainText>
